Q 5.5 — Personnel Monitoring During Setup and Open-Door Interventions (人員監測)

原文內容 Original Text

Q 5.5. When and how should environmental and personnel monitoring be performed during setup and open-door interventions?

Recommendation

All open-door interventions need to be monitored from the point where the first critical surface enters the RABS. The minimum level of monitoring inside a RABS during critical activities is continuous viable and total particle monitoring; continuous viable monitoring is achieved by passive-air and active-air monitoring.

For open-door activities, including line set-up, monitoring within the intervention zone is recommended. This monitoring needs to be based on QRM principles and may need to be changed to ensure monitoring covers the performed activities. Sampling locations, as defined in the EM risk assessment, should be linked to qualified and unqualified interventions.

Additional samples might be taken, based on QRM principles, in the UDAF immediately outside the intervention zone, close to the operator and open-door. This can be achieved with either passive or active monitoring; samples should be taken at the working position level.

Each primary operator involved in open-door interventions, including line setup, should be monitored immediately as they exit the RABS Grade A interior, after having completed all the intervention steps in the critical zone, including any disinfection that may be required. The RABS door disinfection and closure should be done by the secondary operator.

Representative samples should be taken as defined in the risk assessment of the EM program. Sample locations must be selected as per the risk assessment. The risk assessment should consider any body part entering the Grade A environment and any location selected through the risk assessment, and these must meet Grade A limits (e.g., taking samples from the operator's RABS gloves, sleeves, head, and chest, as appropriate to the specific intervention).

It is recommended that a second, fully trained operator should support the monitoring to prevent false positive growth. This sampling should be done in an environment that prevents contamination of the sample (e.g., the UDAF zone of protection or another UDAF zone close to the RABS).

To be representative, samples should be taken as close as possible (i.e., physical and temporal) to the end of the operators' activities inside the RABS. Gowns should be removed and replaced following sampling. Care must be taken to ensure that agar is not transferred to the RABS or surrounding cleanroom where the sampling takes place, during the degowning and gown disposal step.

The individual whose clothing was sampled will then need to leave the cleanroom and replace some or all of their aseptic clothing (i.e., RABS gloves and gown). The second person should also open any doors to allow the person sampled to pass without transferring agar onto cleanroom surfaces.

Rationale

Entry of personnel into the RABS reduces the effectiveness of the barrier and potentially puts the product at risk of contamination. Performing personnel monitoring after, and active air sampling during, the open-door activities provides valuable additional data to support batch disposition.

An approved EM risk assessment should be used to determine the representative locations that require sampling meeting Grade A limits (e.g., body parts entering the Grade A environment). Relying only on glove-sampling data may not be adequate, especially where RABS gloves are disinfected or changed immediately prior to the intervention.

When sampling occurs close to the point where the person exits the RABS, the data collected will most closely reflect the risk posed by the operator to the RABS and will be less influenced by the surrounding lower-grade cleanroom and surfaces outside the RABS that are touched up to the point where the samples are taken. Ideally, a second person would sample the person exiting the RABS at the point they exit, this minimizes any external influences on the data (e.g., handling of plates, pens, documentation in Grade B) and ensures that the samples fully represent the risk posed by the first operator to the critical zone and have not been unnecessarily compromised.

Note: Operators should leave the RABS and change gloves to prevent the spread of media residues after finger dabs.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Intervention Zone (介入區域)：操作人員進行開門介入時所影響的 RABS 內部區域。在此區域內必須進行環境監測。

UDAF (Unidirectional Airflow，單向氣流)：從 HEPA 過濾器垂直向下流動的潔淨氣流，提供 Grade A 等級的空氣品質保護。

Primary Operator vs. Secondary Operator (主操作員 vs. 輔助操作員)：主操作員負責在 RABS 內執行介入操作；輔助操作員負責門的消毒、關閉以及人員取樣，形成「雙人互控」的品質保證機制。

False Positive Growth (假陽性生長)：因取樣技術不當或環境干擾導致的非真實微生物回收。由第二人協助取樣可減少此風險。

比喻說明 Analogy

把開門介入想像成進入無塵室的「安全檢查站」。主操作員就像進入手術室的外科醫師，完成操作後必須在出口接受「感染管控檢查」（人員取樣）。輔助操作員就像門口的感控護理師，負責門的消毒和取樣工作。這是一個「一人做事、一人監督」的雙人機制，確保每次進出都有完整的微生物數據記錄。

重點提示 Key Notes

  • 即時取樣原則：人員取樣必須在操作員離開 RABS Grade A 環境「立即」進行，因為時間延遲會讓結果受到周圍較低級別環境的影響。
  • 全身取樣，不只手套：僅依賴手套取樣可能不足夠，特別是當 RABS 手套在介入前剛被消毒或更換時。應考慮手套、袖套、頭部、胸部等部位。
  • 培養基殘留管控：手指壓印取樣後，操作員必須離開潔淨室更換手套和衣物，防止瓊脂殘留轉移到 RABS 或潔淨室表面。
  • 輔助操作員協助開門：被取樣人員不應自行開門，以避免將瓊脂轉移至門把等潔淨室表面。

實務應用 Practical Application

在 CDMO 環境中，開門介入的人員監測程序是法規查核的重點項目之一。建議建立標準化的「雙人介入 SOP」，明確規定：(1) 主操作員的操作步驟與範圍、(2) 輔助操作員的門管控與取樣職責、(3) 取樣部位與方法清單、(4) 取樣後的衣物更換與培養皿送檢流程。這份 SOP 應包含在 CCS 文件中，並在 APS 期間進行驗證。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為什麼由第二人取樣比操作員自行取樣更具代表性？在數據可靠度方面有何差異？
  2. 如果 RABS 手套在介入前剛做過消毒，為什麼僅取手套樣可能不足以評估操作員帶來的風險？
  3. 人員取樣後為什麼需要完全更換無菌衣物？如果不更換，可能造成什麼後果？
Q 5.6 — Separating EM Data for Setup vs. Filling (EM 數據分離)

原文內容 Original Text

Q 5.6. Should environmental monitoring (EM) for line setup and filling be kept separate?

Recommendation

Yes. While not mandated, there are benefits to keeping EM for line setup and filling separate. Keeping the data from open-door line setup separate aids the investigation and process improvement in the event of EM recoveries (1, 7).

Rationale

Line setup activities usually pose a higher risk to the critical zone because they typically include frequent open-door interventions, material movements into the RABS, and the presence of personnel in the critical zone, whereas filling activities are typically conducted via closed-door interventions. Segregating the two activities for EM allows the data from line setup and filling activities to be visualized and trended independently. Where EM recoveries occur, identifying the assignable root cause of the microbiological data deviation is aided when the data for the two activities are separate.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Line Setup vs. Filling (產線建置 vs. 充填)：這是 RABS 操作中風險等級截然不同的兩個階段。產線建置通常涉及頻繁的開門介入、物料搬入、人員進入關鍵區域；而充填階段通常透過關門介入（使用手套口）進行，風險相對較低。

EM Recoveries (EM 微生物回收)：指在環境監測中偵測到微生物的事件。將建置與充填的 EM 數據分開，可以更精準地追溯污染來源。

比喻說明 Analogy

想像你經營一家餐廳，如果把「備餐時段」和「出餐時段」的食品安全檢驗結果混在一起報告，當發現問題時你就無法判斷是備餐還是出餐環節出了差錯。將兩者分離追蹤，就像分別記錄「廚房準備階段」和「餐廳服務階段」的衛生數據，這樣當出現異常時可以快速鎖定是哪個環節的問題。

重點提示 Key Notes

  • 非強制但強烈建議：文件用「not mandated」但隨即強調「有益處」，這在法規語境中意味著最佳實踐的期望，查核時若未執行需提供充分理由。
  • 趨勢分析價值：分離數據可以獨立觀察產線建置和充填各自的微生物趨勢，對於持續改善 (continuous improvement) 非常有價值。
  • 根因調查效率：當發生 EM 偏差時，分離的數據可以立即判斷問題發生在哪個階段，加速調查進程。

實務應用 Practical Application

對 CDMO 而言，將建置與充填的 EM 數據分離是展示品質管理成熟度的重要指標。建議在 LIMS 或 EM 數據庫中設定「活動階段」標籤，讓每筆 EM 數據都能自動標記為「Setup」或「Filling」。這樣在年度趨勢報告或客戶審計時，可以清楚呈現每個階段的微生物控制水準，也有助於識別系統性改善機會。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為什麼產線建置階段通常比充填階段有更高的微生物污染風險？
  2. 如果一家工廠沒有將建置與充填的 EM 數據分開，在法規查核時可能面臨什麼挑戰？
  3. 在你的 LIMS 系統中，你會用什麼欄位或標籤來實現這種數據分離？
Q 5.7 — Fixed EM Air-Monitoring Sampling Point Locations (固定式 EM 空氣採樣點定位)

原文內容 Original Text

Q 5.7. Where should the fixed environmental monitoring (EM) air-monitoring sampling points be located within the restricted access barrier system (RABS)?

Recommendation

Firms should conduct a risk assessment in the design phase to determine the number and locations of EM samples that should be taken. (See PDA Technical Report No. 13 (Revised 2014): Fundamentals of an Environmental Monitoring Program.)

The sampling locations should be positioned as closely as possible to the most critical operations, such as the point of fill, sorting bowl, or rotary-table. They should be positioned vertically at or close to the height of the critical surface they are monitoring and ideally in the same plane.

Note: FDA's 2004 Guidance for Industry: Sterile Drug Products Produced by Aseptic Processing—Current Good Manufacturing Practice states:

"Air in the immediate proximity of exposed sterilized containers/closures and filling/closing operations would be of appropriate particle quality when it has a per-cubic-meter particle count of no more than 3520 in a size range of 0.5 μm and larger when counted at representative locations normally not more than 1 foot away from the work site, within the airflow, and during filling/closing operations. This level of air cleanliness is also known as Class 100 (ISO 5)."

Sampling locations should not breach First Air over critical surfaces. They should be positioned so that they capture the risks from any permitted intervention, for example, between the RABS door or glove and the critical surface being monitored, and between the door and critical surfaces where open-door interventions are permitted.

Viable- and total-particle sampling locations should be co-located wherever possible (if supported by risk-assessment) both to allow a point of comparison and for ergonomic reasons. Sampling locations should not cause an interference on the airflow between the sampling points (i.e., ideally isokinetic sampling for viable monitoring). AVS should demonstrate the noninterference during the sampling (e.g., passages of RABS gloves during the plate changing).

Total-particle sampling positions need to be set to allow a tube no longer than one meter (1 m) to connect the isokinetic sampling-head to the particle counter. Where lengths greater than 1 m must be used,* studies are required to assess the particle loss, in particular, the 5.0 μm particle loss, and determine if improvements are required. Ideally, the connecting tube would run straight. Any necessary bends should have smooth bend radii, where a 90° bend is achieved over no less than 15 cm of tube.

*Note: RABS should be designed/installed to avoid use exceeding 1 m.

Rationale

It is not possible to monitor the entire RABS. A risk assessment is required to position EM samples in locations where they are most likely to detect the risks posed from the main contamination risks, that is, conducting both open- and closed-door interventions.

Each unique particle size will have a different deposition profile in tubing based on, for example, airflow velocity and sample volume, tubing diameter, sampling port arrangement, temperature, bend radius, tube length, and tubing material. Because particulate monitoring attempts to assess a range of sizes (e.g., 0.5 μm and greater in optical diameter), no single set of radii or length conditions can describe best practices for each of these particle sizes. Minimizing the number of tubing bends, maximizing radii, and minimizing overall tubing length should be the goal, and it should be done in accordance with the particle-counter equipment manufacturer's recommended best practices.

The particle-counter equipment manufacturer should provide technical justification for its recommendations. Instrument calibration should address sampling configuration.

Note:

  • EU Annex 1 now states that tube length should typically be no longer than 1 m and any bend radii should be avoided.
  • International Organization for Standardization (ISO) 14644-1:2015 Cleanrooms and Associated Controlled Environments — Part 1: Classification of Air Cleanliness by Particle Concentration also states that tube length should be no longer than 1 m.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Isokinetic Sampling (等速採樣)：採樣探頭的吸入速度與周圍氣流速度一致，確保粒子被等比例地採集，不會因為速度差異導致取樣偏差。這是微粒監測準確性的關鍵。

Co-location (共位設置)：將微生物採樣點與微粒採樣點設置在同一位置，這樣當某處出現微粒異常時，可以直接比對同一位置的微生物數據，方便關聯分析。

1 m 管路限制：連接等速採樣頭與粒子計數器的管路不應超過 1 公尺。管路越長，粒子（特別是 ≥5.0 μm 的大粒子）因沉降和管壁附著而損失越大，導致測量結果偏低。

Bend Radii (彎曲半徑)：管路如必須彎曲，90° 彎折應在至少 15 cm 的管長上平緩完成，避免急彎造成粒子損失。

比喻說明 Analogy

想像你在一棟大樓安裝火災偵測器。你不能把偵煙器裝在離火源很遠的走廊盡頭 — 應該裝在最可能起火的廚房附近和關鍵出口處。同樣地，RABS 的 EM 採樣點要盡可能靠近灌裝點、分瓶台等最關鍵的操作位置。而管路就像偵煙器的連接線 — 越短、越直，訊號傳遞越準確；彎折太多，「煙」（粒子）就會在途中損失。

重點提示 Key Notes

  • 設計階段就要規劃：採樣點位置應在 RABS 設計階段透過風險評估確定，而不是安裝後才「找空間放」。
  • 位置的三維考量：水平方向要靠近關鍵操作，垂直方向要在關鍵面的高度或接近高度，理想狀態在同一平面。
  • 不能干擾 First Air：採樣點本身不能阻擋保護關鍵面的 First Air，否則就是「為了監測品質而降低了品質」。
  • 在門與關鍵面之間：採樣點應位於 RABS 門或手套口與關鍵面之間，這樣才能捕捉到介入操作帶來的污染風險。
  • 多方法規一致要求 1 m：EU Annex 1 和 ISO 14644-1:2015 都明確要求管路長度不超過 1 m。這已是國際共識。

管路設計關鍵參數 Tubing Design Parameters

管路長度限制：  ≤ 1 m（EU Annex 1 / ISO 14644-1）
90° 彎折最小弧長：≥ 15 cm
FDA ISO 5 微粒限值：≤ 3,520 particles/m³ (≥0.5 μm)
採樣距離：         ≤ 1 foot (~30 cm) from work site

粒子損失影響因素：
  - 管路長度 (tube length)
  - 彎折數量與半徑 (bend count & radii)
  - 管徑 (tubing diameter)
  - 氣流速度 (airflow velocity)
  - 管材 (tubing material)

實務應用 Practical Application

在 RABS 設備採購階段，粒子計數器的安裝位置與管路走向必須列入 URS 和設計確認 (DQ) 文件中。建議與設備供應商確認：(1) 粒子計數器的建議管路配置；(2) 超過 1 m 管路時的粒子損失驗證方案；(3) 採樣頭的等速取樣設計。這些在設計階段確定，可避免安裝後發現管路超長而需要進行昂貴的改裝。同時，AVS 應驗證所有採樣點在運作中（含培養皿更換動作）不會干擾氣流。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為什麼 5.0 μm 粒子比 0.5 μm 粒子更容易在長管路中損失？從物理原理解釋。
  2. 如果你的 RABS 設計中，粒子計數器管路不得不超過 1 m，你需要執行什麼研究來證明測量結果仍然可靠？
  3. 為什麼建議將微生物採樣點與微粒採樣點共位設置？在什麼情況下可能不適合共位？
  4. 採樣點應位於 RABS 門/手套口與關鍵面之間，而不是關鍵面的正上方。請解釋這個定位原則背後的邏輯。

本節重點回顧 Section Summary

  • Q5.1 監測頻率：oRABS 與 cRABS 的 EM 頻率要求完全相同 — 從關鍵面暴露開始到最後一個容器密封為止，必須進行連續微生物與微粒監測。同樣的 EM 計畫適用於生產和 APS。
  • Q5.2 表面監測：應透過風險評估選定監測表面，重點包括直接/間接接觸部件、介入手套、RTP 門、關鍵面上方不可滅菌的部件。表面取樣在批次結束後進行。
  • Q5.3 培養皿轉移：培養皿應透過 RTP、傳遞艙、預先放入或 plate slider 等方式進出 RABS，絕不應在產線建置後為了轉移 EM 培養皿而開門。
  • Q5.4 培養皿存放：存放位置必須遠離 First Air 路徑和關鍵面，不阻擋回風口，使用培養皿架區分已用/未用培養皿，並在 AVS 中驗證。
  • Q5.5 人員監測：開門介入需要即時的人員取樣（手套、袖套、頭部、胸部等），由第二人執行取樣，取樣後須更換衣物並防止培養基殘留轉移。
  • Q5.6 數據分離：雖非強制要求，但強烈建議將產線建置與充填階段的 EM 數據分開追蹤，以利趨勢分析和根因調查。
  • Q5.7 採樣點定位：採樣點應在設計階段定位，盡可能靠近關鍵操作且在同一高度平面，管路長度不超過 1 m，微生物與微粒採樣點建議共位設置。
6

Topic 6: Material Transport

物料傳輸 | p73-p83

PDA Points to Consider No. 12 (2025) — RABS | p73 - p83

本章學習目標

  • 理解間接產品接觸面 (Indirect Product-Contact Surfaces) 的滅菌與去污方法及其在 RABS 中的重要性
  • 掌握膠塞 (Stoppers)、容器 (Containers) 及工具設備轉移進入 RABS 的不同技術與風險考量
  • 學習如何依據物品關鍵性分類（直接/間接產品接觸、破壞 First Air 等）選擇適當的轉移策略
  • 了解建立允許進入 RABS 物料清單的法規要求及污染控制策略 (CCS) 的整合
  • 區分無菌傳遞系統 (Aseptic Transfer Systems) 與人工傳遞系統 (Manual Transfer Systems) 的優缺點
  • 認識 Campaign Manufacturing（連續生產）中間接接觸零件留置的條件與驗證要求

本章導覽 Section Navigation

Q6.1 間接接觸面滅菌 Q6.2 零件批間留置 Q6.3 膠塞轉移 Q6.4 容器轉移 Q6.5 設備工具轉移 Q6.6 物料許可清單
Q 6.1 How should indirect product contact surfaces be sterilized or decontaminated?

Original Text

Recommendation

Indirect product-contact parts such as stopper bowls, hoppers, ancillary items (e.g., tweezers, forceps), and guides must be sterilized (1). This is typically done by wrapping the clean items in suitable semi-permeable packaging material and sterilizing them in a moist-heat autoclave, followed by unloading, transportation through the cleanroom environment, and aseptic assembly inside the RABS. Machine items that break First Air (e.g., sensors, holders, brackets at the filling line or rotary table) should be avoided where possible. When machine items do break First Air, they should be sterilized. (See Question 6.5 for more details.)

Based on facility layout and whether Grade A continuity can be applied for the sterilized items (e.g., by using UDAF carts), either single-wrapping or double-wrapping can be applied to ensure transport of the autoclaved, sterilized parts from the Grade B autoclave to the entrance of the RABS. To provide for aseptic removal and transfer of the parts into the RABS, good aseptic technique must be used to ensure that the inner layer or part is only exposed within the Grade A environment. The wrapping materials and removal process should minimize particle generation as much as possible.

When using double wrapping, the outer wrapping is ideally removed at the barrier door, where the contents are still protected by the inner barrier. For large items, such as the stopper bowl, two people may be needed to properly complete the aseptic transfer. That is, the primary and secondary operators are responsible for different steps: typically, one for the transfer activities outside the RABS, and one for the transfer activities inside the RABS. The inner wrapping is then removed toward the end of the assembly process under Grade A conditions, depending on the design of the manufacturing line just before or after the RABS doors are closed. In case parts of the assembly are done as a closed-door intervention, the wrapping could be removed at an earlier stage to enable removal of the wrap from the RABS just before door closure or as a final open-door intervention. Special considerations must be taken in the sequence of removing the wrapping so as to ensure the First Air of already unwrapped parts is not breached during the removal of other wrappers.

Automated surface bio-decontamination processes such as VPHP, are not considered equivalent to sterilization processes, however, they can reduce bioburden risk if applied after the set-up process is complete and the RABS doors are closed.

If items can be directly unloaded into the cRABS (e.g., via RTP) or an aseptic transfer from the autoclave to the RABS is otherwise guaranteed (e.g., via Grade A continuity, typically a process requiring rigorous controls), different means of wrapping and/or dry-heat sterilization of the indirect product-contact items may be applied. The wrapping materials and removal process should minimize particle generation as much as possible.

In addition to open-door installation, an introduction of indirect product-contact parts via RTP or sterile boxes can be considered for the RABS to minimize the risk of potential contamination during installation by open doors. This especially applies for smaller parts such as guiding and stopper guardrails, for example.

Rationale

Indirect product-contact surfaces are critical for the sterility assurance of the product and must be sterilized (1).

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Indirect Product-Contact Parts (間接產品接觸零件)：這些零件不會直接碰觸藥液，但會接觸到與產品直接接觸的物品，例如膠塞碗 (Stopper Bowl) 接觸膠塞、漏斗 (Hopper) 引導膠塞或容器。因為它們在無菌關鍵區域內運作，仍必須達到滅菌等級。

Single-Wrapping vs. Double-Wrapping (單層包裝 vs. 雙層包裝)：選擇取決於設施佈局是否能維持 Grade A Continuity（A 級連續性）。若從高壓釜到 RABS 入口全程有 UDAF 保護（如使用 UDAF 推車），單層包裝即可；若運輸路徑經過 Grade B 區域且無法保證連續 A 級環境，則需雙層包裝以確保內層在暴露前始終受到保護。

VPHP Bio-decontamination（汽化過氧化氫生物去污）：注意文件明確指出 VPHP 「不等同於滅菌」(not considered equivalent to sterilization)。它可降低生物負荷風險，但不能取代濕熱滅菌。這是一個常見的法規考點。

比喻說明 Analogy

想像你在手術室 (Operating Room) 準備手術器械。手術刀直接接觸傷口（直接接觸），而手術托盤雖然不直接碰觸傷口，但承載著手術刀（間接接觸）。你不會因為托盤「只是間接接觸」就不消毒它 -- 同理，膠塞碗和導軌也必須經過完整滅菌流程。

雙層包裝的概念就像俄羅斯套娃：外層在 Grade B 門口移除（第一層保護脫去），內容物仍受內層保護；內層只在 Grade A 環境內才打開，確保關鍵零件從未暴露於低等級環境。

重點提示 Key Notes

拆包順序至關重要：文件特別強調拆包時必須注意順序，確保已經拆開包裝的零件的 First Air 不會被其他包裝材料的移除動作所破壞。這在實務中是一個常被忽略的操作細節，但卻是稽查時的高風險發現項目。

主要操作員/次要操作員分工：大型零件（如膠塞碗）的無菌傳遞需要兩人配合 -- Primary Operator 負責 RABS 外部活動，Secondary Operator 負責 RABS 內部活動。這種分工設計是為了降低交叉污染風險。

實務應用 Practical Application

在 CDMO 營運中，物料傳遞策略直接影響批次準備時間與污染風險。若新設施設計時能採用 RTP（快速傳遞口）將間接接觸零件直接轉入 cRABS，可大幅減少開門操作次數。雖然 RTP 的初期設備投資較高，但長期來看可降低偏差調查成本、提升批次放行效率，並減少 APS 失敗風險。這是新建廠房的設計決策中值得優先考量的選項。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為什麼 VPHP 生物去污不被視為等同於滅菌？在 RABS 設置完成後使用 VPHP 有什麼價值？
  2. 如果你的設施佈局中，高壓釜與 RABS 之間需要穿越一段 Grade B 走廊（無 UDAF 保護），你會選擇單層包裝還是雙層包裝？為什麼？
  3. 在拆除包裝時，為什麼必須考慮順序而不能同時拆除多個零件的包裝？
Q 6.2 Can stopper bowls, hoppers, and tracks remain installed between batches?

Original Text

Recommendation

If a campaign manufacture has been justified and there is no risk of contamination during and in between the batches, which has been validated in APS, indirect product-contact parts can remain within the RABS system for several batches of a campaign using the same equipment. Typically, after completion of a campaign, the items are environmentally monitored, cleaned, and sterilized before being reused. In addition to the aspect of sterility assurance that the campaign time does not adversely affect particle generation by abrasion from stoppers also needs to be considered.

Rationale

Specific principles may be defined for campaign manufacture if product sterility assurance is not jeopardized (1).

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Campaign Manufacture（連續生產/批次連產）：指使用相同設備連續生產多個批次的同一產品，期間不進行完整的拆裝和重新滅菌。這在 CDMO 中是提升效率的重要策略，但前提是必須證明無菌保證不受影響。

APS Validation（無菌製程模擬驗證）：Campaign 的批間留置必須通過 APS 驗證。APS 需要模擬 campaign 的最長持續時間，證明在整個期間內間接接觸零件仍維持無菌。

比喻說明 Analogy

想像餐廳的鍋具：如果你連續用同一口鍋煮同一道菜的不同批次，中間只需簡單清潔而不必每次都送去高溫消毒。但如果這口鍋要在連續使用中保持安全，你必須先證明：(1) 連續使用不會導致食物殘留累積，(2) 磨損不會產生有害微粒。Campaign manufacturing 的邏輯完全相同 -- 先驗證，後執行。

重點提示 Key Notes

微粒生成 (Particle Generation) 的隱藏風險：文件特別提到膠塞的磨損問題。膠塞在碗和軌道中反覆滑動會產生微粒，Campaign 時間越長，磨損越嚴重。這不僅是無菌問題，也是可見異物 (Visible Particulate) 和不溶性微粒 (Sub-visible Particulate) 的 CQA 風險，必須在 Campaign 時間驗證中評估。

Campaign 結束後的處理：Campaign 結束後，所有留置零件必須經過環境監測 (EM)、清洗和重新滅菌才能再次使用。這確保了任何在 Campaign 期間累積的風險都被完全消除。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 如果你的 CDMO 客戶要求進行為期五天的 Campaign 生產，你在 APS 驗證中需要模擬哪些最差條件 (Worst Case)？
  2. 膠塞碗的磨損產生微粒，這個問題與哪些產品 CQA 直接相關？你會如何設計驗證方案來評估 Campaign 時間上限？
Q 6.3 What approaches are recommended for transferring stoppers into a RABS?

Original Text

Recommendation

There are different ways of transferring stoppers into RABS. Aseptic transfer systems (e.g., RTP) have a lower-risk profile compared to manual transfer systems. New RABS systems preferably should be designed using aseptic transfer systems.

Aseptic Transfer Systems

For sterile ready-to-use stoppers, the stopper transfer can be done by aseptic connector systems using RTPs. To enable this, the RABS will need to be designed with an applicable transfer system close to the stopper hopper. An example of this can be seen in Figure 6.3-1.

Stoppers can then be directly sterilized in the transfer port containers (or as ready-to-use packaging material that has been presterilized by the supplier) and aseptically transferred into the RABS by a closed-door intervention. (The RABS design should facilitate opening the transfer door without overreaching any indirect product-contact parts with the RABS gloves.) The integrity of those rapid transfer bags (e.g., by visual inspection for breaches or defects) or rigid containers (e.g., by regular integrity-testing of the vent filters) need to be assured.

Figure 6.3-1 Rapid Transfer Port (RTP) for Stopper Loading

For processes or facilities where stopper sterilization is undertaken, for instance, in a stopper processor, where stopper sterilization cycles are qualified in a closed stopper pod, stopper transfer can be achieved via a docking mechanism that involves docking of the stopper pod to a stopper transfer chute. The sterilization of the stopper transfer chute and bottom of the stopper pod must be demonstrated, therein providing a sterile passage of the sterilized stoppers directly to the sterilized stopper hopper located in the RABS.

Manual Transfer Systems

Other more manual surface-disinfection systems may be used for transferring stoppers into RABS as well. For example, where the double-wrapped stopper bag is first transferred from Grade B into a Grade A hatch by removal of the outer wrap, the hatch can be closed and then operated by built-in RABS gloves, loading the stoppers via a second hatch and chute into the stopper hopper. Figure 6.3-2 provides a schematic drawing of such a system, detailing the use of a UDAF transfer box to access the inside of the RABS; Figure 6.3-3 provides an example of this system.

Figure 6.3-2 Manual Stopper Transfer System Schematic

Figure 6.3-3 Example of Manual Stopper Transfer System

Open-door interventions, where the RABS door is to be opened for stopper loading, preferably would be avoided by design.

Rationale

Design requirements must be considered for new RABS projects to optimize the aseptic stopper transfer. Aseptic transfer systems are recommended over manual transfer systems to improve contamination control and minimize the risk to sterility assurance.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

RTP - Rapid Transfer Port（快速傳遞口）：一種密封的機械對接系統，允許在不破壞 RABS 屏障完整性的情況下將物料傳入 Grade A 區域。其核心原理是「Alpha-Beta 門」設計 -- 外側（Alpha 門）和內側（Beta 門）各有一道密封門，對接時形成密閉通道，物料通過後兩門分離，各自恢復密封狀態。

Closed-Door Intervention（關門操作）：透過 RTP 或 RABS 手套進行的操作，全程不需打開 RABS 門，維持屏障完整性。這是最優先的操作模式。

Stopper Processor（膠塞處理器）：一種將膠塞清洗、滅菌和乾燥整合在密閉系統中的設備。滅菌後的膠塞 Pod 可直接對接到 RABS 上的傳遞槽，實現全密閉傳遞。

比喻說明 Analogy

把膠塞轉移想像成太空站的對接過程。RTP 系統就像太空船與太空站的對接艙門 -- 兩側各有獨立密封門，對接時形成密閉通道，太空人（膠塞）通過後，雙方重新密封，站內環境從未暴露於外太空（低等級環境）。相比之下，人工傳遞系統更像是穿著太空衣出艙作業 -- 雖然可行，但風險更高、操作更複雜。

重點提示 Key Notes

設計決定命運：文件反覆強調「by design（從設計出發）」這個概念。新建 RABS 系統「preferably should be designed using aseptic transfer systems」-- 這不是建議，而是近乎要求。如果在設計階段沒有納入 RTP，後期改裝將非常困難且昂貴。

避免開門裝載膠塞：開門操作是所有膠塞裝載方式中風險最高的，文件明確表示「preferably would be avoided by design」。這意味著在新廠設計時，若仍規劃開門裝載膠塞，法規稽查員可能會質疑設計合理性。

完整性保證：無論使用哪種傳遞系統，都必須確保傳遞容器的完整性 -- 軟袋需目視檢查破損，硬容器需定期測試通氣過濾器的完整性。

實務應用 Practical Application

作為 CDMO，當你評估新產線的膠塞裝載方式時，應建立一個風險矩陣來比較三種選項：

  • RTP 系統：最低污染風險、可實現 Closed-Door Intervention、初期投資最高
  • 手動傳遞（Grade A Hatch）：中等風險、需要操作員技能驗證、可通過 RABS 手套操作
  • 開門操作：最高風險、需要最多的 EM 監測和人員監測、應僅作為最後手段

在提交設計確認 (DQ) 文件時，必須記錄為何選擇或排除每種方案的理由，這是 CCS 的一部分。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. RTP 系統的 Alpha-Beta 門設計如何確保傳遞過程中 Grade A 環境不被破壞？
  2. 如果你的現有 RABS 沒有 RTP 設計，而是使用 Grade A Hatch 進行手動膠塞傳遞，你需要在 SOP 中規定哪些關鍵步驟來降低風險？
  3. 為什麼文件建議在 RABS 設計中確保「opening the transfer door without overreaching any indirect product-contact parts」？這與 First Air 概念有什麼關係？
Q 6.4 How should bulk containers or ready-to-use containers be transferred into the RABS?

Original Text

Recommendation

Vials are typically washed and introduced into the RABS via a depyrogenation tunnel, which is similar in concept to isolator lines. In contrast to isolator systems, which are placed in a Grade C background where all the equipment might be placed in one room, the washing and tunnel system for RABS are placed in a separate room of a lower classification than the Grade B RABS background and connected through the wall (1, 4).

For ready-to-use packaging material, for example, syringes, vials, and pre-crimped cartridges, there are different technologies that can be used for their introduction into the RABS. Electronic beam (e-beam) technology (Figure 6.4-1) or VPHP (Figure 6.4-2) can be used for a complete-surface decontamination, or a no-touch-transfer (NTT) system (Figure 6.4-3) with multiple overwrap removal, followed by a de-lidding/de-lining process, can be employed.

Figure 6.4-1 E-beam Technology for Introduction of Ready-to-Use Packaging Material

Figure 6.4-2 Vapor Phase Hydrogen Peroxide (VPHP) Technology for Introduction of Ready-to-Use Packaging Material

Figure 6.4-3 No-Touch-Transfer (NTT) Technology for Introduction of Ready-to-Use Packaging Material

NTT applies to double-bagged (secondary packaging) removal via successive debagging steps for the transfer of nested tubs of containers in a sterile barrier into Grade A filling lines without any manual disinfection applied in material transfer. "No touch" denotes there is no physical contact with the contents ejected from the packaging through to the next higher-grade zone, with debagging (cutting a bag open and ejecting the contents) applied as a semi-automated or automated process to reduce operator interventions (19).

Rationale

The transfer of bulk containers must ensure that the open containers are rendered sterile (or remain sterile) and that introduction into the RABS does not lead to contamination of the Grade A environment.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Depyrogenation Tunnel（去熱原隧道）：使用高溫乾熱（通常 ≥250°C）來去除西林瓶上的內毒素（熱原）並達到滅菌效果。這是散裝西林瓶 (Bulk Vials) 進入 RABS 的標準路徑。隧道的出口端直接連接 RABS 的入口端，形成連續的無菌通道。

E-beam（電子束）技術：使用高能電子束對 RTU（即用型）包裝材料的外表面進行完整去污。特點是速度快、不留殘留物，但設備投資較高。

NTT - No-Touch-Transfer（無接觸傳遞）：透過逐層自動化拆袋 (Debagging)，將巢式容器盤 (Nested Tubs) 從多層包裝中取出並送入 Grade A 區域，過程中無人手接觸、無手動消毒步驟。這是最先進的 RTU 容器引入技術。

比喻說明 Analogy

容器進入 RABS 的不同路徑，就像進入手術室的不同消毒通道：

  • 去熱原隧道好比進入手術室前的「火焰消毒走廊」-- 西林瓶通過 250°C 的高溫隧道，所有微生物和熱原都被徹底消除
  • E-beam / VPHP好比「紫外線消毒艙」-- 用能量或化學氣體對包裝外表面進行去污
  • NTT好比層層剝洋蔥 -- 每一層「外衣」（包裝袋）在越來越潔淨的環境中被自動化移除，內容物始終不被碰觸

重點提示 Key Notes

RABS vs. Isolator 的廠房設計差異：文件指出一個關鍵的設施設計差異 -- Isolator 系統可放在 Grade C 背景中，所有設備可在同一房間；但 RABS 的清洗和隧道系統必須放在比 Grade B 更低等級的獨立房間中，並通過牆壁連接。這直接影響廠房佈局和建造成本。

RTU 包材的三種引入技術各有適用場景：E-beam 適合高產量線（速度快但設備貴）；VPHP 適合已有 VPHP 系統的 cRABS；NTT 適合追求最低操作介入的情境。選擇時需考量產量、投資預算和操作複雜度的平衡。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為什麼 RABS 的清洗/去熱原隧道系統需要放在獨立房間而非與 RABS 同一房間？這與 RABS 的 Grade B 背景要求有什麼關係？
  2. NTT 系統中「no touch」的設計理念如何體現了 EU Annex 1 對減少人員介入的要求？
  3. 如果一間 CDMO 同時處理散裝西林瓶和 RTU 預充針，設施設計上需要規劃哪些不同的容器引入路徑？
Q 6.5 How should equipment, accessories, ancillary items and sterile tools be transferred into a RABS?

Original Text

Recommendation

As a general concept, the transfer of all materials and equipment into the Grade B and, finally, the Grade A RABS should be a unidirectional process, separated from the path for removal of those items. Material and equipment introduced, whenever possible, should be wrapped and sterilized, when necessary.

The principles discussed below are based on the criticality of the item regarding product contact.

Direct Product Contact Parts

Direct product-contact parts (e.g., vials, stoppers, piping, single-use systems (SUSs), connectors or components), which have come into direct contact with the product, must be sterilized (1, 4). This is founded on two basic principles:

  • If the filling equipment has CIP and SIP functionality, then the parts can either remain in the RABS or parts of it can be assembled, followed by a validated SIP process, rendering the equipment and filter (where applicable) sterile. (See PDA Technical Report No. 61: Steam in Place for additional information.)
  • If the filling equipment needs to be manually assembled and has no SIP functionality, either presterilized (e.g., gamma-irradiated) single-use assemblies are used, or alternatively, if the filling equipment is sterilized by wrapping the clean items in suitable semipermeable packaging material and sterilized in a moist-heat autoclave, followed by aseptic assembly inside the RABS. If items can be directly unloaded into the cRABS (e.g., via RTP) or an aseptic transfer from the autoclave to the RABS is guaranteed (e.g., via Grade A continuity, typically a process requiring rigorous controls), different means of wrapping and/or dry-heat sterilization of the indirect product-contact items may be applied. Where presterilized, the equipment should be fully assembled (as far as possible) to minimize the need for aseptic connections.

Indirect Product Contact Parts

Indirect product-contact parts (e.g., stopper bowls, hoppers, tweezers), which have come into indirect contact with the product, are to be sterilized and handled in a similar way to direct product-contact parts (1). (See Question 6.1 for more detail.)

Machine Items that Break First Air

Machine items that break First Air (e.g., sensors, holders, brackets at the filling line or rotary table) should be avoided where possible. This must be part of the initial design considerations for a RABS. Where a First Air interruption is not avoidable, machine items should be moist-heat sterilizable. Where this is not technically possible, sporicidal disinfection and a risk assessment of each individual part should be carried out and included in the CCS (1). These parts should have both the highest-possible level of cleanability (preferably with sporicidal agents) and the lowest-possible air interruption (e.g., fewer gaps/holes, be as small as possible, ergonomically shaped). Inclusion in the EM program (e.g., surface sampling at the end of manufacture) needs to be considered.

Miscellaneous Items that Break First Air

Miscellaneous items that potentially break First Air (e.g., forceps for removing stuck stoppers) must be sterile and remain sterile during their intended use inside the RABS. Those items preferably can be sterilized by moist heat and wrapped in semi-permeable packaging, or by dry heat in stainless-steel boxes (care should be applied on appropriate closure of those boxes). Each individual unit should not contain more items than are reasonably needed for the completion of a batch or campaign. To avoid contamination of the sterile items during their intended usage, suitable holders should be designed inside the Grade A space to avoid reaching over the critical parts of the item with the RABS gloves.

Transfer of Items

Methods to transfer wrapped packages into a RABS depends on whether or not the RABS has automated surface-decontamination functionality (e.g., VPHP). If this is the case, the outside surface of packages could be surface-disinfected by the automated process after a transfer through a cleanroom area. If surface-disinfection is purely manual, either an outer-pouch should be removed if the items were sterilized double-wrapped (preferred) or a manual disinfection of the package/wrapping needs to take place when the items enter the Grade A RABS.

Non-Product Contact Equipment and Parts

Non-product-contact equipment/parts (e.g., format parts such as vial guides) are not always suitable for moist- or dry-heat sterilization. Those are parts formally not required to be sterile but must meet Grade A conditions regarding surface cleanliness when inserted into the RABS. Those parts can either be disinfected manually or with the help of automated surface-disinfection processes (e.g., VPHP or similar). When removing the parts from the RABS (if stored outside the RABS without cleaning (i.e., for product dedicated parts)) and before re-usage, the parts should be protected (e.g., by adding a protective pouch) while still within Grade A. If parts are cleaned, they should be protected during storage and before re-usage.

Removal of Items from RABS

Once RABS doors are closed, the removal process of any items from the RABS (e.g., exposed plates or package/wrapping) must not impact the unidirectional airflow protecting direct and indirect product-contact surfaces. In addition, the removal should follow a unidirectional process where the flow of material into the RABS is separated from the flow of items to be removed. For best practice in cRABS, RTPs placed at different and suitable locations may be used to facilitate the transfer of material. Processing and waste-removal flows should be considered during the equipment design and procurement phase, the placement of access ports should be recorded in the equipment User Requirements Specification, and the rationale should be documented in the Design Qualification and/or CCS.

Rationale

Transfer techniques into and out of the RABS are based on the type of material/accessory/equipment, its cleanability and disposal. Either sterilization or surface decontamination is needed.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

物品分類階層（按產品接觸關鍵性）：本題是 Topic 6 中最核心的架構，按照物品與產品的接觸關鍵性分為四個層級：

  1. Direct Product-Contact Parts（直接產品接觸零件）：如管路、充填針頭、SUS 組件 -- 必須滅菌
  2. Indirect Product-Contact Parts（間接產品接觸零件）：如膠塞碗、鑷子 -- 必須滅菌（同直接接觸零件處理）
  3. Machine Items Breaking First Air（破壞 First Air 的機械零件）：如感測器、支架 -- 應優先設計避免，無法避免時需滅菌或殺芽胞消毒 + 風險評估
  4. Non-Product Contact Parts（非產品接觸零件）：如容器導軌 -- 不需滅菌但須符合 Grade A 表面清潔度

Unidirectional Process（單向流程）：物料進入和移出 RABS 必須走不同路徑，防止「乾淨」物料與「污染」廢棄物交叉。這是 GMP 廠房設計的基本原則。

比喻說明 Analogy

把 RABS 想像成一座高度管制的機場。每種「旅客」（物品）根據其「安全等級」（產品接觸關鍵性）需要通過不同的安檢程序：

  • VIP（直接接觸零件）：必須通過最嚴格的安檢（滅菌），攜帶特殊通行證（滅菌包裝）
  • 商務旅客（間接接觸零件）：安檢程序同等嚴格（同樣需滅菌）
  • 一般旅客（破壞 First Air 的零件）：能不進來最好不進來（by design avoid），若必須進來則需最高級別安檢
  • 機場工作人員（非產品接觸零件）：不需 VIP 級安檢，但必須穿著乾淨制服（Grade A 表面清潔度）

而且，所有人的入口和出口必須分開（Unidirectional Process），就像機場的入境和出境走不同通道。

重點提示 Key Notes

「By Design Avoid」原則：對於破壞 First Air 的機械零件，文件的立場非常明確 -- 首選方案是在設計階段就消除它們。這體現了 EU Annex 1 強調的「Quality by Design」理念：與其事後管控風險，不如從源頭消除風險。

Sporicidal Disinfection（殺芽胞消毒）的特殊地位：當無法避免且無法滅菌的零件破壞 First Air 時，必須使用殺芽胞消毒劑（而非普通消毒劑）。原因是 Grade A 區域的微生物控制目標是零生長，而普通消毒劑可能無法殺滅芽胞形態的微生物。

廢棄物移出的設計考量：文件要求在設備設計和採購階段就考慮廢棄物移出流程，包括 RTP 的位置規劃。這些必須記錄在 URS（使用者需求規格）和 DQ（設計確認）中。很多問題都源於設計階段的疏忽。

實務應用 Practical Application

在 CDMO 的日常營運中，Q6.5 所描述的分類架構可以直接轉化為一份「物料傳遞矩陣表」(Material Transfer Matrix)，列出每一類物品的：

  • 分類等級（直接/間接/破壞 First Air/非接觸）
  • 滅菌/消毒方法
  • 包裝方式（單層/雙層）
  • 傳遞路徑（RTP/Hatch/開門）
  • 移出方式

這份矩陣表應成為 CCS 的附件，並作為新人培訓和稽查準備的核心文件。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為什麼預滅菌的設備應「盡可能完整組裝」(fully assembled as far as possible)？這與減少無菌連接 (Aseptic Connections) 的風險有什麼關係？
  2. 一個旋轉台上的感測器支架破壞了 First Air 但無法進行濕熱滅菌。根據本文的指導，你需要執行哪些步驟來管控這個風險？
  3. 為什麼非產品接觸零件（如容器導軌）從 RABS 中移出時需要在 Grade A 環境中加上保護套？它們不是不需要無菌嗎？
Q 6.6 Is having an approved list of material that is permitted to enter the RABS required?

Original Text

Recommendation

An approved list of material and equipment must be established for all items to be transferred into Grade A and Grade B areas. As part of the CCS, all materials allowed to be transferred into the RABS need to be predefined, including a description of how it is transferred (1). During shut-downs or maintenance stops, where the RABS and cleanrooms are not in an operational state, additional tools, equipment, and material might be brought into the RABS, and those must be controlled through other means of the quality system (e.g., change management, maintenance work orders).

Rationale

Control steps are to be implemented for all material that is about to be transferred to the aseptic environment.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Approved Material List（核准物料清單）：這是一份正式受控文件，明確列出所有允許進入 RABS 的物料、設備和工具。每個項目都必須包含「如何傳遞」(how it is transferred) 的描述。這份清單是 CCS 的組成部分，等同於 RABS 的「入場許可名冊」。

Change Management（變更管理）：在停機或維護期間，可能需要將清單外的工具或設備帶入 RABS。這些例外必須通過品質系統的正式變更管理程序來控制，不能臨時決定、隨意引入。

比喻說明 Analogy

核准物料清單就像高安全級別大樓的「訪客白名單」。只有名單上的人（物料）才能進入，每個人的進入方式（走正門、走側門、需要護送）都有明確規定。如果有不在名單上的訪客（如維修工人）需要進入，必須走特殊審批程序（變更管理），而不是讓門衛自行決定。這確保了每次進入都有記錄、都經過評估，沒有「臨時加碼」的空間。

重點提示 Key Notes

「Must」而非「Should」：注意文件使用「must be established」-- 這是強制要求而非建議。EU Annex 1 (2022) 在第 4.3 節中明確要求 CCS 涵蓋所有可能影響無菌性的因素，包括進入無菌區的物料管控。缺少核准物料清單是稽查中常見的重大發現。

停機/維護期間的管控不能放鬆：很多廠區認為停機期間可以放寬物料管控，但文件明確指出即使在非營運狀態下，進入 RABS 的額外物品也必須通過品質系統控制。這是因為維護期間引入的污染可能在恢復生產後影響產品品質。

實務應用 Practical Application

一份完整的核准物料清單應包含以下欄位：

此清單應定期審查（建議每年至少一次），並在任何新增物品時觸發變更管理流程。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 如果稽查員要求你展示「進入 RABS 的物料如何被控制」，你需要準備哪些文件？
  2. 維護團隊需要將一台新的校正儀器帶入 RABS 進行感測器校正。這個動作需要經過哪些品質系統程序？
  3. 核准物料清單與 CCS 之間是什麼關係？為什麼 PDA 將其定位為 CCS 的一部分？

本節重點回顧 Section Summary

  • 物品分類決定管控策略：所有進入 RABS 的物品依據其產品接觸關鍵性分為四個層級（直接接觸/間接接觸/破壞 First Air/非接觸），每個層級對應不同的滅菌或消毒要求。間接接觸零件的管控等級等同於直接接觸零件。
  • 設計決定命運（By Design）：無論是膠塞傳遞（優先選用 RTP）還是消除破壞 First Air 的零件，最佳策略都是在設計階段就做出正確決定。後期改裝的成本和風險遠高於前期設計投入。
  • 單向流程 (Unidirectional Flow) 是基本原則：物料進入和廢棄物移出 RABS 必須走分離的路徑，防止交叉污染。這必須在設備 URS 和 DQ 中記錄。
  • Campaign Manufacturing 的條件：間接接觸零件可在批間留置，但必須通過 APS 驗證 Campaign 全程的無菌保證，並評估膠塞磨損產生的微粒風險。
  • 核准物料清單是強制要求：作為 CCS 的一部分，必須建立正式清單列出所有允許進入 RABS 的物料及其傳遞方法。停機維護期間的額外物品也需通過變更管理控制。
  • VPHP 不等同於滅菌：自動化生物去污可作為補充措施降低風險，但不能替代對產品接觸零件的正式滅菌。
7

Topic 7: Cycle Development

週期開發 | p84-p89

PDA Points to Consider No. 12 (2025) — RABS | p84 - p89 | Q7.1 - Q7.3

本章學習目標

  • 理解 RABS 清潔與消毒程式規劃、設計與執行的關鍵考量因素
  • 掌握手動消毒與自動化生物去污染 (Bio-decontamination) 之間的差異與應用場景
  • 了解消毒劑確效 (Disinfectant Qualification) 的方法論，包含 BI 挑戰試驗與 EI 相關性研究
  • 認識 RABS 清潔、消毒與去污染確效的完整架構，以及如何與 CCS、EM 和 APS 銜接

本章內容導覽

Q7.1 清潔與消毒計畫 Q7.2 一致性執行與確效選項 Q7.3 確效與驗證要求
Q 7.1 Cleaning and Disinfection Program Planning

原文內容 Original Text

Q 7.1. What are the considerations for planning, designing, and executing a restricted access barrier system (RABS) cleaning and disinfection program?

Recommendation

Before implementing a cleaning and disinfection program, a RABS cleanability assessment should be performed. This assessment should include the suitability of material surfaces to be cleaned as described in Question 1.2. In addition, cleaning accessibility in terms of ergonomics, the extent of reach required into the RABS, and areas that need cleaning tools to reach should be considered. Hard to clean mechanical spaces and surfaces in processing areas should have been eliminated by design as a basic GMP requirement (4). As disinfection programs must include the use of an approved sporicidal, the materials of construction within the RABS should be assessed to be compatible with such disinfectant agents.

*Note: Sensitive equipment (e.g., environmental monitoring equipment) must be considered during cleaning, disinfection and/or decontamination and may need to be covered at a certain cleaning step. This should be documented in the CCS.

Typically, RABS will include installed process equipment (e.g., filling lines) that are also subjected to cleaning and disinfection together with the RABS barrier. Cleanability assessments will therefore include suitability and access of process equipment surfaces for cleaning and disinfection procedures.

Cleaning is a prerequisite to effective bio-decontamination processes. Initially, at start-up and after shutdowns, a cleaning agent with a surfactant will assist with the removal of bonded layers of soiling (e.g., lubricants, grease, fatty acids from human contact). Cleaning agents are likely to leave residues that may require a follow-up wipe removal step with sterile 70% IPA for example, and such actions should be included in SOP control design (1, 6).

Agents will be validated to demonstrate the appropriate log reduction, including bacteria, spores, and viruses (as required), with the target of achieving Grade A conditions in the RABS. The process in which agents are manually applied must be qualified to ensure appropriate environmental conditions are rendered (6). RABS Grade A conditions must be established and under control before sterilized parts, including fluid path or filling needles and indirect product-contact parts (e.g., stopper bowls, guides, chutes), are introduced (1).

Bio-decontamination processes (e.g., VPHP, dry or wet process technologies) should be automated; an emphasis should be on a validated cleaning process prior to initiating the bio-decontamination process.

More automated bio-decontamination processes (e.g., VPHP, dry or wet process technologies) may be applied to oRABS (in combination with cleanroom) and cRABS. If disinfection cannot be implemented manually (i.e., considered in design), and if enhanced sporicidal efficacy and disinfection assurance is required.

In such applications, cleaning is not replaced by automated disinfection alone and remains an essential pre-step. In first application or following shutdowns cleaning, where more surface-soiling may be present, a neutral detergent with a surfactant may be appropriate, but inevitability it will leave residues, so a following residue-removal step would be required, typically with isopropanol.

A cleanability assessment, selection of cleaning and disinfectant agents, and associated methods of application should be defined in a cleaning risk assessment to cover the risk-based decision-making requirement as part of the QRM. Having a rationale in place, a qualification methodology can be developed ahead of qualification protocols and execution.

Manual Cleaning and Disinfections of RABS

RABS require cleaning and disinfection to establish and maintain Grade A conditions. Manual processes for these steps are described below.

Cleaning is the removal of soiling, residual product, and nonviable contaminants. The process is typically manual, completed with wipes that apply cleaning agents and a physical removal (i.e., collection in a wipe) of contaminants (1, 6).

Disinfection is a process of applying, via a qualified procedure, a laboratory-validated disinfectant that provides an appropriate log reduction of bioburden to specified levels. All disinfection programs for RABS should include a sporicidal agent (1, 6). Appropriate residue removal is required after cleaning using purified/sterile water (e.g., WFI) or sterile isopropanol.

There are two stages of RABS disinfection:

  1. Establishing control of the Grade A processing environment on first installation, after shutdown, and between batches and campaigns. This first step of disinfection should include a sporicidal agent, hence, sporicidal disinfection of the complete internal processing area within the RABS.
  2. Routine disinfection in production, which includes after open-barrier interventions and wiping down the barrier door before closing. The selection of the disinfectant should be based on a risk assessment and assurance that Grade A conditions are not compromised.

It is recommended that primary and secondary operators carry out these disinfection tasks related to interventions. Interventions into Grade A processing zones should be undertaken by a primary operator with the necessary localized internal-zone disinfection followed by personnel monitoring, based on an approved risk assessment, prior to closing the operations. The secondary operator should complete the internal RABS door disinfection before closing the RABS barrier.

Rationale

If RABS are cleaned and disinfected by manual application methods, the prerequisite of a cleanability assessment is paramount.

Different combinations of cleaning and disinfectant agents may be applied based on process steps and levels of soiling.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Cleanability Assessment (可清潔性評估): 在任何清潔消毒程式實施之前，必須先進行系統性的可清潔性評估。這不僅是評估表面材質是否適合清潔，更重要的是評估人體工學上操作者能否有效地觸及 RABS 內部所有區域。這個步驟常被忽略，但它是整個清潔確效的基礎。

Sporicidal Agent (殺孢子劑): EU Annex 1 明確要求 RABS 的消毒程式必須包含殺孢子劑。這是因為細菌孢子是最難殺滅的微生物形態，也是無菌保證最大的威脅。常用的殺孢子劑包括過氧化氫 (H2O2)、過氧乙酸等。

Log Reduction (對數降低): 衡量消毒劑效力的標準指標。例如 6-log reduction 代表將微生物數量從 1,000,000 降至 1，即 99.9999% 的殺滅率。

比喻說明 Analogy

想像你要清潔一間手術室。你不會直接噴消毒水就開始手術 — 你必須先做「可清潔性評估」：哪些角落容易藏污？設備底部碰得到嗎？清潔工具夠長嗎？這就像 RABS 的 Cleanability Assessment。接著，你先用清潔劑去除可見的髒污（Cleaning），然後再用消毒劑殺菌（Disinfection）。順序絕不能顛倒，就像你不會在滿是油漬的桌面上直接噴酒精消毒一樣 — 油漬會阻擋消毒劑接觸表面，效果大打折扣。

重點提示 Key Notes

清潔永遠是消毒的先決條件！ 本節反覆強調 "Cleaning is a prerequisite to effective bio-decontamination processes"。這是因為表面殘留物（潤滑劑、油脂、人體接觸殘留的脂肪酸）會形成保護層，降低消毒劑的效力。

兩階段消毒策略：

  • 第一階段（建立控制）： 首次安裝、停機後、批次/製程轉換時 — 必須使用殺孢子劑對 RABS 內部全面消毒
  • 第二階段（日常維護）： 生產中開門介入後、關門前擦拭 — 消毒劑選擇基於風險評估

Grade A 必須先建立： 在將已滅菌零件（如充填針頭、膠塞斗）引入 RABS 之前，Grade A 條件必須已經確認建立且受控。

操作人員分工 Operator Roles

文件特別提到 Primary Operator（主要操作員）和 Secondary Operator（次要操作員）的角色分工：

  • 主要操作員： 負責 Grade A 區域的介入操作，以及介入後的局部消毒與人員監測
  • 次要操作員： 負責 RABS 門內側的消毒與關門操作

這種雙人互相監督的設計，是為了確保消毒程序的完整性和可追溯性。

實務應用 Practical Application

在 CDMO 環境中，當你接手一條新的 RABS 產線或準備上新產品時，清潔消毒程式的規劃是無法跳過的關鍵步驟。常見的失誤包括：

  • 設備設計時未考慮清潔可及性，導致某些死角根本無法手動清潔
  • 使用的殺孢子劑與 RABS 內部材料不相容，造成腐蝕或表面損傷
  • 清潔劑殘留未有效去除，影響後續消毒效果

因此，在 RABS 採購階段就應將 Cleanability Assessment 納入設計審查 (Design Review)。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為什麼清潔 (Cleaning) 必須在消毒 (Disinfection) 之前執行？如果順序顛倒會有什麼後果？
  2. 在什麼情況下，自動化生物去污染 (如 VPHP) 會比手動消毒更適合 RABS？
  3. 為什麼敏感設備（如 EM 設備）在清潔消毒時需要特別保護？這應記錄在哪個文件中？
Q 7.2 Consistent Execution of Cleaning, Bio-Decontamination, and Disinfection

原文內容 Original Text

Q 7.2. What are the current options for ensuring consistent execution of cleaning, bio-decontamination, disinfection, and sporicidal disinfection of a restricted access barrier system (RABS)?

Recommendation

Disinfectant agents will require qualification or validation to provide evidence of efficacy on surfaces for a defined contact time, typically referred to as "wet contact time" (2). Different disinfectant qualification methodologies can be applied based on the best combination of international standards and guidance.

Aseptic-process filling would require Grade A particulate and microbial cleanliness levels inside the RABS, with cleaning and disinfection considered as the surface-contamination control measure (1). The outside of the RABS barrier would require following the cleanroom grading level (in filling Grade B).

Disinfectant agents are validated for efficacy in laboratory studies, including material coupon surface-disinfection studies, with subsequent qualification of the application method and procedure. EM is used to assess the effectiveness of the cleaning and disinfection program (1, 6). In-field efficacy challenge studies are not typically implemented for manual disinfection applied to RABS in contrast to automated VPHP process technologies, bio-decontamination, and alternative sporicidal-agent processes that require biological-indicator (BI) inactivation challenge studies (4).

The bio-decontamination processes of VPHP process technologies have the potential of achieving 6-log reduction when combined with the required qualification of the automated gaseous-disinfection system and method of application with associated control parameters (6). Once the bio-decontamination-equipment integration is qualified, a process of cycle development should be applied, followed by an efficacy-performance qualification (PQ) with a BI reference challenge of Geobacillus stearothermophilus spores on stainless coupons. VPHP BI's are described in PDA Technical Report No. 51 Biological Indicators for Gas and Vapor-Phase Decontamination Processes: Specification, Manufacture, Control and Use.

Enzymatic indicators (EIs) are increasingly playing a role in cycle development to improve efficiency (time savings) and assessment of location-to-location efficacy. However, accepting the initial BI/EI correlation studies is required, and the final cycle qualification currently requires BI challenge studies.

The outcome of manual disinfection, following the application of a qualified agent according to a qualified SOP, is assessed by the EM program. The EM program assesses the effectiveness of the qualified disinfection and bio-decontamination process. RABS cleaning and disinfection qualification should align with ISO 14644-1 requirements for cleanrooms and associated controlled environments and with EU Annex 1 and FDA guidances on manufacturing sterile products by aseptic processing for qualification before conducting APS qualification in readiness for production activities.

Open-door interventions into a RABS barrier during aseptic processing, a rare occurrence, requires additional cleaning and disinfection of the open barrier door, including the inside of the barrier door, before it is closed to reestablish Grade A conditions of the complete barrier. Protective airflow and procedure control should result in the sterilized parts that enter during setup remaining sterile without compromise. Disinfection applied to sterile surfaces could potentially compromise sterility and therefore should be avoided, instead focusing on the procedural control and protective airflow that prevents compromise to the sterile surfaces in the first place.

Rationale

Primarily, RABS are manually cleaned and disinfected using qualified agents and a qualified procedure of application of these qualified agents executed by trained operators. EM, in combination with other microbial challenges (e.g., gowning, material transfers, and environmental control systems), is used to monitor the outcome (effectiveness).

Some of the enhanced attributes in contamination control that isolators provide, are sometimes applied to RABS to enhance the assurance of sterility. In particular, cRABS and oRABS (in combination with cleanroom) with VPHP can align elements of isolators and RABS technology.

The combined cleanroom and oRABS bio-decontamination, using an automated process, can support more assured aseptic hold times and fast changeovers to reestablish the required conditions for aseptic manufacturing. Such processes can be applied, with BI results (negative for growth) defined as the marker, to put the line back in operation at risk, rather than waiting for EM results.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Wet Contact Time (濕潤接觸時間): 消毒劑必須在表面保持濕潤狀態的最短時間，才能達到宣稱的殺菌效力。這不是「噴上去等它乾」，而是要確保整個接觸時間內表面都是濕的。在大面積 RABS 內部進行手動擦拭時，這是最大的操作挑戰之一。

Biological Indicator, BI (生物指示劑): 使用已知數量的高抗性微生物孢子（通常是 Geobacillus stearothermophilus）來挑戰消毒/去污染製程的效力。BI 是 VPHP 週期確效的「金標準」。

Enzymatic Indicator, EI (酶指示劑): 較新的技術，利用酶活性的變化來快速評估去污染效力。EI 的最大優勢是結果更快（數分鐘 vs. BI 的 7 天培養），可大幅加速週期開發階段。但最終確效仍需 BI 挑戰。

比喻說明 Analogy

想像手動消毒 RABS 就像用濕拖把拖整棟房子的地板 — 你可以做得很好，但結果取決於拖把是否乾淨、地板是否先掃過、你是否真的拖到了每個角落、以及地板是否保持夠久的濕潤。而 VPHP 自動化去污染就像是整棟房子放煙霧彈式的殺蟲 — 氣體會均勻擴散到每個角落，效果更一致、更可靠。但即使用了煙霧彈，你仍然要先把地板掃乾淨（清潔仍是前提！）。

重點提示 Key Notes

手動 vs. 自動化的確效差異：

  • 手動消毒： 實驗室確效 (coupon study) + 應用方法確效 + EM 監測結果評估。不需要 in-field BI 挑戰。
  • VPHP 自動化： 實驗室確效 + 設備整合確效 + Cycle Development + PQ（含 BI 挑戰）。需要 6-log reduction 證明。

關鍵警告 — 不要對已滅菌表面消毒！ 文件明確指出 "Disinfection applied to sterile surfaces could potentially compromise sterility"。這是因為消毒擦拭的動作本身會引入污染風險，反而不如維持氣流保護和程序管控來得安全。

RABS 與 Isolator 的融合趨勢

Rationale 中提到一個重要的產業趨勢：cRABS 和 oRABS 正在借鑑 Isolator 的 VPHP 技術。這種「混合型」方案帶來兩大實務優勢：

  • 更可靠的無菌保持時間 (Aseptic Hold Time)： 自動化去污染提供比手動消毒更高的保證
  • 更快速的批次轉換 (Changeover)： BI 結果（無菌）可作為重新開線的依據，不需等待 EM 結果（通常需 5-7 天）

對 CDMO 而言，這意味著更高的產線利用率和更快的交付時間。

公式與計算 Formula

6-log Reduction 的意義：

初始孢子數: 10^6 = 1,000,000 CFU
6-log reduction 後: 10^0 = 1 CFU
殺滅率 = 99.9999%

實務意義：
- 若 BI 上接種 10^6 個 G. stearothermophilus 孢子
- VPHP 週期後 BI 培養結果必須為「無生長」
- 這是 PQ 通過的判定標準

實務應用 Practical Application

BI vs. EI 的實務決策： 在 CDMO 中進行 VPHP 週期開發時，EI 可以大幅縮短開發時間。典型的週期開發流程為：

  • 使用 EI 快速篩選不同的 VPHP 參數組合（H2O2 濃度、溫度、暴露時間）
  • 找到最佳參數後，執行 BI/EI 相關性研究（Correlation Study）
  • 最終 PQ 仍以 BI 挑戰（G. stearothermophilus, 10^6 孢子）為判定標準

另外，文件提到可以用 BI 結果（陰性）作為 "at risk" 重新開線的依據，而不必等 EM 結果。這在多產品 CDMO 中是一個重要的產能優化策略。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為什麼手動消毒不需要 in-field BI 挑戰，而 VPHP 需要？兩者的確效邏輯有何根本差異？
  2. 為什麼不應該對已滅菌的表面進行消毒擦拭？這違反了什麼核心原則？
  3. cRABS 搭配 VPHP 的「混合型」方案，在什麼類型的 CDMO 場景中最具價值？試從產能與無菌保證兩方面分析。
  4. EI 的結果能否取代 BI 作為 PQ 的最終判定標準？為什麼？
Q 7.3 Qualification and Validation of Cleaning, Disinfection, and Decontamination

原文內容 Original Text

Q 7.3. What considerations are required for qualification of the restricted access barrier system (RABS) cleaning, bio-decontamination, disinfection, and sporicidal disinfection process, and validation of the bio-decontamination and decontamination process?

Recommendation

The qualification of the RABS cleaning and disinfection process is critical to ensuring a Grade A environment within the RABS. The planning of the qualification should begin as early as possible prior to implementation. A key output of the design phase of a RABS installation is a quality risk assessment detailing the RABS physical attributes and usage scenarios that may have an impact on product quality. This risk assessment then feeds into a validation plan of which cleaning and disinfection validation is a major component.

There are different facets to the RABS cleaning and disinfection (bio-decontamination) and decontamination validation process:

  • Establishing Grade A conditions for aseptic manufacturing
  • Applying cleaning validation for drug-product residue removal as a cross-contamination control measure

Decontamination may be applied as a cross-contamination control measure and/or a measure to manage operator exposure to toxic or biologically hazardous products. Where aseptic-containment is required to process toxic or biohazard products, it may be more appropriate to apply isolator barrier technology because of the inherent limitations of containment measures (e.g., air-overspill to the surrounding environment) in RABS.

RABS Cleaning Process

The qualification of the RABS cleaning process should provide confidence of the:

  • Removal of any residue (chemical, including lubricants) or debris that would detrimentally impact the effectiveness of the disinfecting agent to be used. The target should be visibly clean (1).
  • Reduction of bioburden before the disinfection process step, as determined by the end-user.

RABS Disinfection Process

The qualification and validation of the RABS disinfection process should provide confidence that the disinfection procedure demonstrates its effectiveness in reducing any microbiological contamination within the RABS to an acceptable level. The disinfection process should include:

  1. Use of a sporicidal agent, possibly in rotation with other disinfectant agents that together provide broad spectrum efficacy (7). The selection and frequency of use should be based on EM data (quantitative/qualitative), trends, cleanroom materials, and the efficacy of the disinfectant procedures (2).
Note: Rotation of the disinfectants is not considered due to increasing microbial resistance but because different disinfectants have different modes of action, and their combination can increase the spectrum of efficacy. Rotation may also reduce occurrence of material damage.
  1. Use of sterile disinfectant agents for Grade A and Grade B areas.
  2. A target log reduction for bacteria, spores, and viruses (if applicable) (6, 20).
  3. A method of application that assures surface coverage and wet contact time.
  4. A disinfection waste management procedure dealing with wipes, residual agents, and disinfection tools.
  5. Any associated aseptic RABS hold-time qualification.
  6. Environmental control/EMPQ should be qualified and established before implementation of an APS; confidence that the cleaning and disinfection process meets this objective of environmental control is critical to GMP compliance (4).

RABS Decontamination Process

The qualification and validation of a RABS decontamination process applied post-production for product-residue removal as a cross-contamination control measure requires cleaning-validation studies. The following are points to consider:

  • Cleaning methods may be manual (wiping) or more automated CIP systems (e.g., spray balls, spray wands). In both cases, the target is to remove residual products from surfaces.
  • Cleaning validation includes surface-swabbing studies and chemical analysis to confirm removal of product residuals to target levels considered as safe exposure to operators and/or not at risk of cross-contaminating other products or subsequent batches.
  • Where more automated CIP systems apply, control system development will be required with subsequent qualification.

WFI may be used as an agent for product-residual removal for treatment off-line:

  • Chemical agents that denature products in RABS may need a follow-up residue removal step.
  • If CIP systems are applied, sloping surfaces and "zero" dead-leg valves may be required to mitigate collected water that may exacerbate microbial contamination or proliferation.
Note: Disinfectant efficacy studies or validation studies should be conducted as well to demonstrate that the disinfectants used on surfaces in manufacturing areas, laboratories, and other facility areas are effective in the inactivation or removal of such microorganisms as bacteria, fungi (yeast and molds), and bacterial spores. (See PDA Technical Report No. 70: Fundamentals of Cleaning and Disinfection Programs for Aseptic Manufacturing Facilities for further details.)

Rationale

The primary purpose of a RABS is to provide people-operator and process-product-barrier separation so that the risk of contaminating sterile product is mitigated to acceptable levels. As such, it is important to determine the most appropriate bio-decontamination method for the RABS. The qualification and validation of the bio-decontamination methods should consider the cleaning agents, the cleaning application processes, and the associated processes and equipment risks. These requirements and processes should be documented and proceduralized for repeatability and monitored to ensure continuous compliance.

Strong process understanding is the best basis for determining RABS validation requirements. Robust monitoring and aseptic manufacturing processes will add to the confidence that the manufacturing process is under a state of control. Decisions should be made based on the facilities process, control structure, and process understanding. Based on those decisions, validation programs should be initiated and followed. Decisions on the frequency of revalidation should be included in the bio-decontamination validation program.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Validation Plan (確效計畫): RABS 清潔消毒確效不是一個獨立活動，而是整體 RABS 安裝確效 (Installation Qualification) 的重要組成部分。它源自設計階段的品質風險評估 (QRA)，並與設備確效、環境監測確效、APS 確效環環相扣。

Cross-contamination Control (交叉污染控制): 除了建立無菌環境，RABS 的清潔確效還有第二個重要目的：去除前一批產品的殘留物，防止交叉污染。這在 CDMO 多產品共線生產的場景中尤其關鍵。

Visibly Clean (目視潔淨): 清潔確效的最低標準。雖然聽起來簡單，但在 RABS 透過手套操作的情境下，如何確認所有表面都達到「目視潔淨」是一個實際挑戰。

比喻說明 Analogy

RABS 確效的三層架構就像一棟大樓的維護管理：

  • 清潔 (Cleaning) = 日常打掃： 去除灰塵、垃圾、可見污物。標準是「看起來乾淨」
  • 消毒 (Disinfection) = 定期消毒： 用殺菌劑殺滅微生物。目標是達到特定的微生物降低水準
  • 去污染 (Decontamination) = 深度清潔/化學去除： 換住戶（換產品）時，確保前一位住戶的所有痕跡都被清除，新住戶不會接觸到殘留物

三者的目的不同，方法不同，確效要求也不同 — 但都必須做到位。

重點提示 Key Notes

消毒劑輪換的真正原因： 許多人誤以為輪換消毒劑是為了防止微生物產生抗藥性。文件澄清了這個常見誤解 — 輪換的原因是：

  • 不同消毒劑有不同的作用機制 (mode of action)，組合使用可擴大殺菌譜
  • 輪換也可以減少對 RABS 材料的損害（長期使用單一強效消毒劑可能腐蝕某些材質）

確效七大要素 Seven Elements of Disinfection Validation

本節列出了 RABS 消毒確效必須涵蓋的七個面向，這是一個非常實用的檢查清單：

  1. 殺孢子劑的使用（含輪換策略）
  2. Grade A/B 區域使用無菌消毒劑
  3. 目標 log reduction（細菌、孢子、病毒）
  4. 確保表面覆蓋率與濕潤接觸時間的方法
  5. 消毒廢棄物管理程序
  6. 無菌保持時間 (Aseptic Hold Time) 確效
  7. EM/EMPQ 必須在 APS 之前完成

毒性/生物危害產品的限制

文件特別指出，當需要處理高毒性或生物危害性產品時，RABS 的密封性 (containment) 存在固有限制（如空氣外溢至周圍環境），此時更適合使用 Isolator 技術。這對 CDMO 的設備選型策略有重要影響：如果客戶產品組合中包含 ADC、高效能藥物或活性生物製劑，在選擇 RABS 或 Isolator 時需將此因素納入考量。

去污染 (Decontamination) 確效要點

去污染確效與消毒確效的目的不同 — 它針對的是產品殘留物的去除，是交叉污染控制的核心：

  • 方法： 手動擦拭或自動化 CIP 系統（噴球、噴棒）
  • 確效手段： 表面擦拭取樣 (Swab Study) + 化學分析，確認殘留量低於安全暴露限值
  • CIP 設計注意： 斜面設計和零死角閥門，防止積水造成微生物孳生

WFI 可用於產品殘留去除。若使用會使蛋白質變性的化學劑，需額外進行殘留去除步驟。

實務應用 Practical Application

CDMO 多產品轉換場景： 假設你的 RABS 產線剛完成一個單株抗體產品的充填，下一批是胰島素。你需要的確效資料包括：

  • 清潔確效： 表面擦拭後，前一產品的殘留量低於 PDE/ADE 限值
  • 消毒確效： 確認 Grade A 環境重新建立
  • 設備目視檢查： 確認所有表面達到 "visibly clean" 標準

若你的 RABS 搭配 VPHP，可以在清潔後執行自動化去污染週期，用 BI 結果作為放行依據，大幅縮短批次轉換時間。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 消毒劑輪換的主要目的是什麼？它與「抗藥性」的關係為何？
  2. 為什麼 RABS 對高毒性/生物危害產品的適用性有限？Isolator 在這方面的優勢是什麼？
  3. 在 RABS 去污染確效中，表面擦拭取樣 (Swab Study) 的目的是什麼？它驗證的是哪個風險？
  4. 為什麼 CIP 系統需要斜面設計和零死角閥門？積水會帶來什麼風險？

本節重點回顧 Section Summary

  • 清潔是一切的前提： 無論手動消毒或自動化 VPHP，清潔 (Cleaning) 永遠是消毒/去污染的必要先行步驟，不可被取代或跳過
  • 兩階段消毒策略： 第一階段建立 Grade A 控制（含殺孢子劑全面消毒），第二階段為日常維護（介入後局部消毒）
  • 手動 vs. VPHP 的確效路徑不同： 手動依賴實驗室確效 + EM 監測；VPHP 需要完整的 Cycle Development + BI 挑戰 PQ（6-log reduction）
  • EI 加速開發但不能取代 BI： 酶指示劑可加速週期開發效率，但最終確效判定仍需生物指示劑挑戰試驗
  • 確效是系統工程： 清潔/消毒確效源自設計階段的 QRA，並與 EM 確效、APS 確效形成完整鏈條，必須在 APS 之前全部到位
  • 去污染針對交叉污染： 不同於消毒（針對微生物），去污染旨在去除前批產品殘留，是多產品共線生產的關鍵控制措施
  • RABS 的密封限制： 處理高毒性或生物危害產品時，因 RABS 的空氣外溢風險，應考慮採用 Isolator 技術
8

Topic 8: Aseptic Process Simulation

無菌製程模擬 | p90-p94

PDA Points to Consider No. 12 (2025) — RABS | p90 - p94 | Q8.1 - Q8.4

本章學習目標

  • 理解 RABS 環境中 Aseptic Process Simulation (APS) 的特殊設計考量與先決條件
  • 掌握多班次與長期 campaign 生產模式下 APS 的關鍵模擬要素
  • 學會如何以風險評估為基礎，定義 RABS APS 的 worst-case 條件
  • 瞭解 RABS 充填線 setup 與 assembly 的最佳實務，以及 open-door 與 closed-door 階段的風險控制

本章內容導覽

Q8.1 APS 特殊考量 Q8.2 多班次/Campaign APS Q8.3 Worst-Case 條件 Q8.4 Setup 與 Assembly 最佳實務
Q 8.1 — APS in RABS: Special Considerations

Original Text

Q 8.1. What are the special considerations for aseptic process simulation (APS) in a restricted access barrier system (RABS)?

Recommendation

A risk-based analysis and approach taken for APS are recommended for all aseptic processing technologies, including RABS systems. By design, the APS should imitate routine manufacturing conditions and should ensure that all critical steps are challenged. A RABS relies on the surrounding cleanroom environment to maintain Grade A conditions for sterile processing. To maintain Grade A, the RABS routinely includes cleaning and disinfection processes, in addition to sterilization processes for processing accessories and equipment. By design, the RABS should only provide for open-door intervention during setup and, by exception, during operations. The cleanroom qualification, operator training, cleaning, and disinfection programs should all be qualified.

There are several key considerations that need to be established in support of APS, and they should include, but are not limited to:

  • Cleanroom and clean air equipment, such as UDAF units, must be qualified according to the required characteristics of the environment.
  • The RABS must be qualified to meet all requirements for aseptic processing including HEPA-filter integrity-testing, pressure differential across the filters, air velocity testing, and AVS. AVS should confirm unidirectional airflow that sweeps over and away from exposed products during processing, without increased risk of contamination through turbulent airflow. Airflow visualization qualification and monitoring should be applied at open-door interventions as a prerequisite to all APS designs to ensure environmental-control conditions are qualified in readiness for an APS.
    Note: APS cannot be used to justify poor design of equipment and processes.
  • Operator training and qualification extending to Grade A and Grade B aseptic gowning and aseptic behavior training must be complete. Operators undertaking RABS cleaning and disinfection programs should be qualified and operations should be implemented procedurally.
  • A list of authorized inherent and corrective interventions should be designed, defined, and appropriately assessed and documented in the CCS to minimize the risk of contamination. Open-door interventions should be a rare and exceptional occurrence. When required, the need to take representative sterility samples should be considered, and the intervention should be effectively demonstrated in an APS.
  • Qualified methods are in place for the transfer of materials that enter the cleanroom, and subsequently the RABS, that do not compromise the cleanroom-surrounding environment or the RABS Grade A processing zone.
  • Risk assessments support the establishment of a comprehensive EM program, which should be based on detailed knowledge of the process, facility, and equipment. Sampling locations, sampling frequency and type of EM monitoring (e.g., active air, passive, contact plate) should be defined based on risk assessment output.

The use of a "piggyback" APS can be considered as part of the overall APS design. A piggyback APS is where an APS run is undertaken at the end of a routine single or campaign filling process and can be used in support of validating an extended run or campaign length/duration. There are specific limitations associated with a piggyback APS which, by design, does not provide for an appropriate simulation of activities and variables that are only performed for the first lot of a campaign, for example, setup activities. Consideration also needs to be given to potential interferences of residual product with the growth-promoting properties of the media used in the APS. Consequently, a piggyback APS alone will not fulfill the validation requirements to demonstrate an effective APS program. Rather, its use can be considered as part of an overall effective APS program, which also must include an APS strategy that covers setup and other potential worst-case scenarios.

The scheduling of piggyback APS in conjunction with traditional APS should be supported by a formal risk assessment, for which the limitations of the piggyback approach and its use are considered.

Rationale

The planning of open- and closed-door interventions and simulation of worst-case criteria should be based on risk management principles. The same criteria for the design of an APS as stated in PDA Technical Report No. 22 (Revised 2011): Process Simulation for Aseptically Filled Products are also appropriate for all RABS.

After establishing Grade A conditions inside a RABS, the barrier technology provides a physical and aerodynamic barrier to contamination ingress to Grade A when the barrier is closed. The barrier is open at setup where presterilized materials are transferred and are installed. At this time, both Grade A conditions and the sterilized parts are at an increased risk for contamination and, thus, can compromise sterility.

If rare open-door interventions take place during aseptic manufacturing, there is also a risk escalation that needs mitigation by design, qualifications, and procedural controls, and is subject to additional qualification in an APS. Such in-process significant interventions require consideration for sterility samples to be taken and should be included in the APS.

Simulation of the production activities is a necessity for designing the APS studies.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Aseptic Process Simulation, APS (無菌製程模擬)：以培養基取代實際藥品，模擬整個無菌充填過程，驗證系統在正常與最差條件下，能否維持無菌保證 (Sterility Assurance)。APS 本質上是對「整個無菌製造系統」的一次綜合性能力測試。

Risk-Based Analysis (基於風險的分析)：APS 的設計不是隨意的，而是以品質風險管理 (QRM) 為驅動。需先識別哪些步驟具有最高的污染風險，再據此設計模擬方案。這也呼應了 EU Annex 1 對 Contamination Control Strategy (CCS) 的核心要求。

Piggyback APS (搭便車式 APS)：在常規生產批次結束後，緊接著執行一次 APS。優點是可驗證延長生產時間或 campaign 長度的能力。但其重大限制在於：它無法模擬 setup 階段的活動（因為 setup 只發生在 campaign 的第一批），所以不能單獨使用，必須搭配傳統 APS 一起構成完整的驗證方案。

比喻說明 Analogy

想像你是一位飛行員，APS 就像是飛行模擬器測試。你必須在模擬器中重現所有可能遇到的情境：正常起降、惡劣天氣、引擎故障等。RABS 的 APS 也是如此 -- 你不僅要模擬正常充填，還要模擬 open-door intervention（相當於緊急降落程序）、setup（相當於起飛前檢查），以及所有可能的worst-case 情境。

而 Piggyback APS 就像是在一次正常飛行結束後，順便進行額外的模擬測試 -- 你可以測試「長時間飛行」的耐力，但你無法從中驗證「起飛前完整檢查程序」是否正確，因為你已經飛在空中了。

重點提示 Key Notes

APS 的六大先決條件：在執行 APS 之前，以下所有項目都必須已完成確效/確認：

  1. 潔淨室確效 -- UDAF 設備符合環境要求
  2. RABS 確效 -- HEPA 完整性、壓差、風速、AVS 全部合格
  3. 人員訓練 -- Grade A/B 無菌更衣與無菌行為訓練完成
  4. 介入清單 -- 固有/矯正介入已定義並納入 CCS
  5. 物料傳遞方法 -- 已確效且不會危及 Grade A 環境
  6. EM 計畫 -- 基於風險評估建立完整的環境監控方案

特別注意原文的警語："APS cannot be used to justify poor design of equipment and processes." -- APS 是用來驗證良好設計的有效性，而不是用來為不良設計找藉口。

法規連結 Regulatory Link

本節參考了 PDA TR No. 22 (Revised 2011)：Process Simulation for Aseptically Filled Products，這是 APS 設計的核心指引文件。此外，EU Annex 1 (2022) 第 9 章對 APS 有詳細要求，包括最少充填量、頻率、以及對 worst-case 條件的模擬要求。

實務應用 Practical Application

假設你是一家 CDMO 的驗證主管，客戶要求使用 RABS 充填線進行 3 天 campaign 生產。你的 APS 方案設計必須考慮：

  • 傳統 APS 至少一次，涵蓋完整 setup 與 closed-door intervention 模擬
  • 可考慮增加 Piggyback APS，在實際生產結束後接續執行，以驗證延長生產時間的能力
  • 兩種 APS 的搭配使用需有正式的風險評估文件支持

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為什麼 RABS 比 Isolator 更需要關注 open-door intervention 的 APS 模擬？
  2. 如果一家公司只執行 Piggyback APS 而沒有傳統 APS，在稽核時可能會被提出什麼缺失？
  3. AVS 為什麼被列為 APS 的先決條件之一？試從氣流與污染控制的角度說明。
Q 8.2 — APS for Multiple Shifts and Campaign Production

Original Text

Q 8.2. What are the special considerations of the aseptic process simulation (APS) for multiple shifts and multiple-day campaign production in the restricted access barrier system (RABS)?

Recommendation

The duration of the APS should be based on risk assessment and sufficient to adequately challenge the aseptic process. The duration should be long enough to allow simulation of the predetermined interventions and activities and to fill the required units.

Where there are no risk-based time-related effects and where longer duration does not pose a risk to the routine production process, there is no requirement that the APS should be equal to or longer than the maximum production duration.

The following points need to be considered when creating an APS for campaign manufacturing:

  • Setup
  • Number and duration of interventions based on risk management principles to ensure that the APS is representative of the routine manufacturing process and qualified interventions (type, frequency, and duration)
  • Indirect product-contact parts remain installed for the duration for requalification of the campaign and are subject to an aseptic hold time (the duration may need to be shortened based on the risk assessment evaluation)
  • Replacement or leaving in place of direct product-contact parts (i.e., product filling needles), should be representative of the routine manufacturing process exposure time
  • RABS gloves remain installed for the duration of the campaign
  • Cleaning/disinfection practices occurring inside the RABS during routine campaign manufacturing should be simulated
  • Certain circumstances when performing an APS related to a production hold and/or interruptions
  • Taking of sterility samples after significant critical interventions, if justified

The approach to APS with a "piggyback" qualification is not considered a best practice as setup is missing in the final APS and not representative of the full campaign.

Rationale

Contamination of an aseptic process is primarily an outcome of events rather than time. Therefore, the duration of the APS should be sufficient to assess the performance of those activities identified in the risk assessment as having the potential to introduce contamination.

The APS is not sensitive enough to uncover the flaws, weaknesses, or failures in the integrity of the RABS, the environmental quality, or the ability of the personnel to perform activities over time.

The APS should challenge and confirm the effectiveness of these contamination control measures. This means that the maintenance of environmental conditions should be assured and assessed by the RABS system design and EM. Good process design and well-controlled activities required between the batches within a campaign (e.g., fill needles or glove replacement), RABS gloves ergonomics, training and qualification of personnel, assessment of human factors, and scheduling of breaks and rest periods for operators are better tools for controlling the complexity of RABS campaign operations than extended APS runs.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Campaign Manufacturing (連續生產/戰役式生產)：指在不進行完整清潔和重新 setup 的情況下，連續生產多個批次的模式。在 RABS 中，這意味著某些零件（如間接接觸產品的零件）在整個 campaign 期間保持安裝狀態。

"Events Rather Than Time" (事件而非時間)：這是本節最重要的觀念 -- 污染主要是由「事件」（如介入、物料傳遞、人員操作）造成的，而不是單純因為「時間長」就會污染。因此，APS 的時長不需要等於或超過最長生產時間，關鍵是要充分模擬所有可能引入污染的「事件」。

Direct vs. Indirect Product-Contact Parts：

  • Direct (直接接觸產品零件)：如充填針頭 -- 在 campaign 中可能需要更換，APS 應模擬這種更換操作
  • Indirect (間接接觸產品零件)：如導軌、stopper bowl -- 在整個 campaign 期間保持安裝，受 aseptic hold time 限制

比喻說明 Analogy

Campaign 生產的 APS 設計，就像規劃一次長途公路旅行的安全測試。你不需要實際開完全程 3,000 公里才能證明車子安全，但你需要模擬旅途中所有關鍵事件：加油停靠（相當於 batch 間的操作）、換輪胎（相當於更換充填針頭）、長時間駕駛後的疲勞管理（相當於操作員輪班和休息安排）。重點不是開了多少公里，而是有沒有把所有可能出問題的「事件」都測試到。

重點提示 Key Notes

Campaign APS 的必模擬項目清單：

  1. Setup 階段 -- 包含初始 open-door 活動
  2. 介入操作 -- 類型、頻率、時長均須代表性
  3. 間接接觸零件 -- 模擬完整 campaign 期間的安裝狀態與 hold time
  4. 直接接觸零件 -- 模擬是否更換或保留（如充填針頭）
  5. RABS 手套 -- 整個 campaign 期間保持安裝
  6. 清潔/消毒 -- 模擬批次間的常規清潔消毒操作
  7. 生產暫停/中斷 -- 模擬計畫性或非計畫性停頓
  8. 無菌取樣 -- 重大介入後的取樣程序

常見誤區 Common Misconception

許多公司誤以為 APS 必須跑得和實際生產一樣長。原文明確指出：「there is no requirement that the APS should be equal to or longer than the maximum production duration」。APS 的目的是驗證「事件管控能力」，而非「時間耐受力」。時間相關的控制（如環境維持、手套完整性、人員疲勞）應由其他工具（如 EM、設備確效、人因評估）來保障。

實務應用 Practical Application

一家 CDMO 的 RABS 充填線進行 5 天 campaign（每天 2 班），共生產 10 個批次。APS 設計考量：

  • APS 時長不需要 5 天，但需模擬所有關鍵事件
  • 包含完整 setup + 至少模擬「批次間」的清潔消毒轉換
  • 充填針頭若每 2 天更換一次，APS 需包含此更換操作
  • 模擬操作員輪班交接的程序
  • 在適當時機取 sterility sample（如重大介入後）

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 原文說「contamination is primarily an outcome of events rather than time」，這句話對你設計 APS 時長有什麼啟示？
  2. 為什麼 Piggyback APS 在 campaign 模式下「不被視為最佳實務」？它具體缺少了什麼？
  3. 如果 campaign 期間 RABS 手套破損需更換，這個事件應該如何在 APS 中處理？
Q 8.3 — Worst-Case Conditions in RABS APS

Original Text

Q 8.3. What are the special considerations for determining worst-case conditions in a restricted access barrier system (RABS) aseptic process simulation (APS)?

Recommendation

Based on the features of the operation, the worst-case scenarios chosen for inclusion in an APS should be predefined. The best way to determine the suitable worst-case scenarios is to evaluate the APS, taking into account the pertinent elements of the process and the aseptic process risk assessment. The worst-case condition should be considered within the expected operational boundary. Worst-case does not mean creation of artificial conditions or environments that exceed allowed operating conditions and can force a system failure.

"Note: APS is not used to validate bad practices."

A few examples of worst-case conditions include, but are not limited to:

  • Open-door interventions (if required) in addition to the setup
  • Closed-door interventions (inherent/corrective)

The following parameters generally have a lower impact on the product-contamination risk, since the Grade A RABS interior environment with exposed product/critical surfaces are separated from the lower-classified environment and operators:

  • Hold time of sterile materials (e.g., filtration and filling equipment, filtered media solution, sterile garments/goggles)
  • Filling duration
  • Simulation of the maximum or minimum number of personnel
  • Speed of the filling machine (i.e., slowest speed for largest container considering the maximum-duration vial remains open online and the highest speed for the smallest container considering difficulties in handling)

Any intervention required via opening the door shall be considered along with the frequency and duration for the simulation in the APS.

Interventions that do not require handling via an open door but need manual adjustment via RABS gloves and tools shall be simulated in a similar way.

A risk-based approach shall be followed in order to determine the frequency, duration, and criticality of the intervention.

Rationale

Open-door interventions represent the highest risk for product contamination and therefore should be the focus of the predefined worst-case conditions in the APS. In addition, the design, barrier properties, and the closed-door interventions of RABS might provide other worst-case conditions, which should be considered in the design of APS. Companies should conduct thoughtful risk assessments to help determine which conditions and configurations represent the most useful challenge to the process and how to most effectively include them in the APS.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Worst-Case Conditions (最差條件)：在 APS 中模擬的「最具挑戰性」的操作條件。但有一個非常重要的界限：worst-case 必須在允許的操作範圍內，不能人為創造超出正常操作邊界的條件來強制系統失敗。

RABS 的 Worst-Case 分層：

比喻說明 Analogy

定義 worst-case 就像消防演習的情境設計。你會模擬「最困難但合理的逃生情境」，例如：電梯故障、某條走廊被煙霧阻擋。但你不會模擬「整棟大樓瞬間倒塌」，因為那超出了合理預期的範圍。

同樣地，RABS APS 的 worst-case 應該模擬「open-door intervention」（最高風險事件），但不應該人為創造一個不可能在正常操作中出現的極端條件（例如同時打開所有門並關閉所有氣流）。

重點提示 Key Notes

RABS 獨特優勢 -- 某些傳統 worst-case 參數影響較低：

與傳統開放式無菌充填不同，RABS 的物理屏障將產品/關鍵表面與操作員和低等級環境隔開。因此，以下參數在 RABS 中的影響顯著降低：

  • Hold time (保留時間) -- 滅菌物料在屏障內受保護
  • 充填時長 -- 屏障關閉時環境控制穩定
  • 人員數量 -- 操作員在屏障外，不直接暴露產品
  • 充填速度 -- 雖仍需考慮（最慢/最快），但影響較傳統系統低

這是 RABS 相較於傳統無菌充填的一個重要風險降低優勢，也是選擇 RABS 技術的商業價值所在。

兩句警語 Two Warnings

原文重複強調了兩個關鍵原則：

  1. "APS is not used to validate bad practices" -- APS 不是為不良操作背書的工具
  2. "Worst-case does not mean creation of artificial conditions...that can force a system failure" -- worst-case 不等於人為製造系統崩潰

這兩句話為 APS 設計劃定了明確的邊界：APS 驗證的是「在合理操作範圍內，系統能否維持無菌保證」。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為什麼 open-door intervention 是 RABS APS 中「最高風險」的 worst-case 條件？試從屏障完整性的角度解釋。
  2. 某公司在 APS 設計中同時模擬「最慢充填速度 + 最多人員 + 最長 hold time」。根據本節內容，這種設計是否合理？為什麼？
  3. 「APS is not used to validate bad practices」這句話在實務上如何應用？請舉一個具體例子。
Q 8.4 — Setup and Assembly Best Practices

Original Text

Q 8.4. What is the best practice when performing the setup and assembly of a restricted access barrier system (RABS) filling line?

Recommendation

There are two setup conditions for RABS: Initially, with an open barrier door, and then, readiness for production operations with the barrier door closed where full EM is implemented and critical tasks involving sterilized parts are completed, for example, positioning of filling needles (if single-use). As much as possible, set-up should be performed with the doors closed so careful design and understanding of the equipment is essential.

The open-door set-up process presents the highest risk of contamination when transferring in or assembling sterilized parts or components.
